## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (mathematical biology) — population dynamics / growth models
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time derivative of population size P(t), which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics (ordinary differential equations) in ecology. Typical relationships express per-capita growth as a function of density P and/or time t (environmental forcing), plus optional mortality/harvest terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net constant influx/outflux added to intrinsic growth)
- Self-limiting (quadratic crowding): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (crowding increases mortality; equivalent to logistic after re-parameterization)
- Power-law density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric or phenomenological growth where per-capita rate scales with P**(c1-1))
- Gompertz growth (logistic in log-space): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (density dependence via log(P); c1 typically relates to 1/K)
- Theta-logistic (generalized logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible density dependence; c2 tunes curvature/strength)
- Allee effect (strong Allee with carrying capacity): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (growth negative at low P; crowding negative at high P)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (net growth reduced by proportional removal; can represent exploitation or predation mortality)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed quota removal; can induce collapse at low P)
- Saturating per-capita growth (resource-limited uptake surrogate): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P) / (c1 * P + c2) - c3 * P (birth saturates with density-dependent limitation plus linear death)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P - c4 * P**2 (periodic environment modulates growth; crowding still acts)
- Long-term trend in environment (nonstationary r): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P - c2 * P**2 (gradual change in intrinsic growth over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth interpretation: writing (dP_dt)/P helps—if it is approximately constant, expect dP_dt ∝ P (exponential regime).
- Carrying capacity behavior: presence of a negative P**2 term (or P*(1 - c*P)) typically implies a stable equilibrium near P ≈ 1/c.
- Gompertz signature: a P*log(P) term implies per-capita growth declines approximately linearly with log(P), often fitting asymmetric sigmoids in P(t).
- Allee signature: a factor like (c*P - 1) or (P - A) implies negative growth below a threshold (bistability/extinction risk).
- Harvesting diagnostics: an additive negative constant term (−c) indicates quota harvest; a negative linear term (−c*P) indicates proportional harvest/mortality.
- Seasonality/forcing: sinusoidal dependence on t in the coefficient of P suggests periodic cycles in growth rate; it can create oscillations even without predator-prey variables.
- Nonstationarity: coefficients that vary with t (e.g., c0 + c1*t) indicate changing environment or management; trends can shift equilibria over time.
- Density-dependence curvature: replacing (1 - c*P) with (1 - (c*P)**theta) changes how sharply regulation turns on; theta > 1 delays regulation until higher P.
- Saturating birth or limitation: rational forms in P (e.g., (c*P)/(c*P+c0)) indicate diminishing returns with increasing P, often proxying resource limitation without explicit resource variables.

I need to analyze whether any candidate can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.1728*(1 - P/48.55)*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(-0.924 + P)))`

This simplifies to:
- Term 1: `0.1728*P - 0.003559*P²` (a linear + quadratic in P)
- Term 2: `0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*P + 1.408))` (a sigmoidal term)

The GT has:
1. A **P²** term
2. A **P** term  
3. A **sigmoidal** term: `P/(1 + exp(linear in P))`

The key structural feature is the **sigmoid function** `P/(1 + exp(...))`. This is NOT a rational function, NOT a power law, NOT a polynomial, and NOT expressible as combinations of `P^c`, `1/(P+c)^n`, `exp(P*c)`, `log(...)`, or `t`-dependent terms.

Let me check what basis functions the candidates use. All candidates are combinations of:
- `P²`, `P` (polynomial terms)
- `P^c` (power law terms)
- `1/(P+c)^5`, `1/(P+c)^2`, `1/P^n` (rational terms)
- `t`-dependent terms (which can be zeroed)
- `exp(P*c)` (some candidates)
- `log(P*c + 1)` (Candidate 50)
- Constants

**Critical question:** Can any combination of these basis functions exactly reproduce `P/(1 + exp(a*P + b))`?

The sigmoid `P/(1+exp(f(P)))` is a fundamentally different function. It:
- Is smooth and bounded
- Has a specific S-shaped transition
- Cannot be decomposed into polynomials, power laws, or rational functions of finite degree

**Candidates with `exp(P*c)`** (5, 19, 29): These have `c4*exp(P*c5)` which is a pure exponential, not a sigmoid `P/(1+exp(...))`. A sigmoid cannot be written as a sum of a pure exponential and rational/polynomial terms.

**Candidate 50** has `log(P*c6 + 1)` - logarithmic, not sigmoidal.

**For all candidates with only polynomial, power-law, and rational terms:** By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, no finite combination of `P^a`, `1/(P+c)^n` terms can exactly equal a sigmoid function for all P.

**t-dependent terms:** The GT has no `t` dependence. Candidates with `t` terms can zero those coefficients, but this doesn't help create the sigmoid.

**Conclusion:** None of the candidates contain the structural element `P/(1 + exp(...))` or any equivalent sigmoidal basis function. The sigmoid function is linearly independent from all basis functions present in the candidates (polynomials, power laws, rational functions, pure exponentials, logarithms). Therefore, no candidate can exactly match the GT.
